<review>If I could give zero stars I would. My father and I came here for lunch after his radiation treatment, he was craving pho so we picked this place because it was close to home. When we got there the place was not packed at all, there were max 5 tables occupied, we sat down and immediately our order was taken, which not bad in my opinion but that's as good as it got. We then were reseated for an unknown reason by the waiter and waited over 30 minutes for our food that never arrived. During this time three more tables were filled and their food brought to them within 10 minutes. We asked the waiter when our food would get to us and his response was you ordered already? We ended up walking out because of the poor service. I understand if orders get forgotten or delayed but to just flat out ignore your customers sitting in the middle of everyone and not ask how they are or if they had ordered yet for over 30 minutes is just wrong and speaks a lot about the care they put into their business. What else do they ignore or forget about I wonder? We will not be coming here again, nor recommend this place to anyone. In addition to the great food...we felt as if we had been invited to
a family home where the food and hospitality was all about

<userid>104600150006171765694</userid>< user_name>
Sam Khandelwal< /user_name>
< Date>
1552674271851</Date>
< Rate>
5</Rate>
<review>We were on the hunt for a quick bite on our way to Sierra Hot Springs in Sierraville north of Tahoe. As expected we got caught in early afternoon Bay Area traffic, and needed a bite for early dinner.

We had heard of hole in the wall Indian restaurants in the Sacramento region. And good ole Yelp lead the way to Curry Paradise, a Pakistani restaurant (similar to North Indian cuisine). Google reviews confirmed this place is legit.

This restaurant is set beside a subway and gas station and has ample parking outside.

The owner from Lahore in Pakistan was super friendly and guided us on our menu selection. While the buffet was a great deal at $9.99, we wanted something custom made.

The owner recommended chicken kebab (yes they are know for their kebabs) for my wife. She taught that was some of the best chicken kebab - and this isn't some white girl who doesn't know her Indian, but a white girl married to an Indian, who knows his Indian. She gave it five stars. Although the owner recommended beef or goat kebab, which he claimed are even better.

We also ordered a plate of Pakoras (veggie fritters dipped in chickpea batter), which were excellent. Not too oily, crisp and with the right amount of spice.

For my main, I wanted their best cottage cheese (paneer) entree. The owner recommended two - saag paneer and paneer tikka masala. I opted for the latter with garlic naan. He made is extra spicy per my request. Delicious. The quantity was enough to become a leftover meal for another day.

The owners wife popped out from behind the kitchen and my wife asked about chai. She said don't have the chai by the buffet, and she would make a fresh pot. She asked me if she should make white girl chai (easy on the masala) and I said give it a desi twist, as my wife can handle more spices than I can. As it turns out, the chai was delicious. And I know my chai. My wife felt this was better than 90% of the chai's she's had in her trips to India. I concur. It was milky, spicy. Tip: Ask for desi masala chai at Indian restaurants to avoid getting plain chai that has minimal masala (spices).

The owners were awesome and said they had recently taken over the restaurant and revamped the menu. They are proud of their home cooked style and specialize in kebabs. In fact they were scrambling to fill an order for 150 plates of kebab for an event, but they spent enough time chatting with us and making us feel welcome.

I would visit them again for their delicious food, warm hospitality and great prices (decent quantity too).

Be a neighborhood hero, supplier your local small business owners.< /review><pics>None</pics>< Resp>
None</Resp>

< review>
Very nice and hip interior design and decorations. The seatings look great although at the curved booths, our party of 4 found it uncomfortable to sit, being squeezed in and awkward feeling.

The food selection is good although pricy. That being said, they have very creative presentations of dishes, using ceramic figures that blow steam. Great for IG pics.

And the service for 90% of the staff is very attentive and kind. I only docked 1 star because one of the staff got my order wrong and indignantly insisted it wasn't.

Overall a great place for friends and hanging out over good food.<//review>

<user_name>Amy Palmer< /user_name>< gmap_id>
0x80857851b0e45d77:0xfb3a73c52a5be6ce< /gmap_id>
< Text>
7/17/13

Right before arriving at Playland-Not-At-The-Beach, my husband had a sudden craving for chicken that he HAD to satisfy. Weird.

There were 3 of us in the car and none had ever been to a Church's before. The drive-thru was like any other, but the menu was new to me! I wasn't at all hungry but I had to try SOMETHING! So I tried the Cajun rice (side) and one piece of crispy chicken. Husband had a chicken sandwich with fries and a drink. Food came pretty quick and I asked for hot sauce, but it was already in the bag. Sweet. Wish I had a couple extra packets. It was pretty good stuff!  My piece of chicken was crunchy and good. I liked the crispy breading but it was a little greasy for me after a few bites. Good flavor though. I don't know how to explain the cajun rice. It was like a mash of rice and meat. We all agreed there was meat in the rice. It's probably my fault for not knowing that cajun rice has meat, but I didn't want unidentifiable meat (or any meat for that matter) in my rice so I tossed this.

Husband's sandwich lasted about as long as my rice. He took a few bites and then took a look inside. The patty just looked really unappetizing. It was a grey-ish color in the middle and something just wasn't right.  His fries ended up in my lap at this point as he tried to wash away all the bad with his giant soda. I decided to abandon my piece of chicken after viewing his. I'd return here, but only for the hot sauce.< /Text>

< Review>
I was giving a talk nearby at the Kaiser center and stopped here for lunch. So glad I did. This location is small and so is the parking lot. We barely found parking and due to the lunch hour rush, the line was long but moved quickly.

The menu isn't very extensive. I had the chicken caesar wrap with garlic fries. My wrap was wonderfully fresh and seasoned and the dijon mustard added a great spicy kick.

Sadly there aren't too many locations in SoCal but I could definitely eat here regularly. It stands apart from most fast food places.</Review>
